## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, which is the core object in reaction kinetics ODE models. Typical relationships express consumption/production rates as functions of A (mass-action orders, saturation/inhibition, reversible approach to equilibrium) and sometimes explicit time dependence (e.g., catalyst decay or forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order decay (mass-action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay / radioactive-like kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or A + A process)
- General n-th order power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order kinetics)
- First-order formation toward a source level: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (relaxation toward steady-state concentration c1)
- Linear production–consumption balance: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant input with first-order removal; chemostat-like lumped kinetics)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-like) rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with limiting capacity)
- Reversible first-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to distance from equilibrium A=c1)
- Mixed-order (parallel paths): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular loss)
- Saturation-limited consumption (enzyme/active-site limitation, non-Michaelis form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at -c0 for large A)
- Substrate inhibition / high-A slowdown: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1 + c2 * A**2) (rate rises then decreases at high A)
- Time-varying effective rate constant (catalyst deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (apparent first-order rate weakens with time)
- Externally forced or periodic conditions: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (baseline decay with time-dependent driving)
- Stretched-exponential kinetics (distributed rates): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (effective first-order with time-dependent hazard)
- Piecewise/activated kinetics (induction time): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) (slow start-up then approaches first-order)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption vs production sign: negative dA_dt typically indicates depletion of A; positive terms often indicate inflow/formation or relaxation toward a setpoint c1.
- Order inference from scaling: if dA_dt / A is approximately constant, first-order is likely; if dA_dt / A**2 is constant, second-order is likely; in general log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) slope suggests order.
- Approach-to-equilibrium behavior: dynamics that slow as A approaches a nonzero level often fit dA_dt ∝ -(A - c1), indicating a stable equilibrium at A=c1.
- Parallel pathways: curvature changes with A can indicate additive loss terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2), where different terms dominate in different concentration regimes.
- Saturation at high concentration: if |dA_dt| plateaus as A increases, use rational forms like -c0*A/(A+c1) rather than pure power laws.
- High-concentration inhibition: if |dA_dt| increases then decreases with A, include inhibitory denominators with higher powers of A (e.g., A + c1 + c2*A**2).
- Time-varying rate constants: if early-time kinetics differ systematically from late-time at similar A, include explicit t dependence (e.g., exp(-c*t), t**c).
- Induction periods: near-zero early rates followed by acceleration can be captured by multiplicative activation factors in time (1 - exp(-c*t)) or similar.
- Source/sink balance: persistent nonzero dA_dt when A≈0 suggests a production term (e.g., +c0), while rapid decay near A≈0 suggests higher-than-first-order loss is unlikely.
- Stiff initial transients: very large |dA_dt| at early times with quick stabilization often indicates strong linear relaxation or large effective c0 in -(A-c1) or -c0*A forms.

**GT: `-0.19494*A + 0.24819*cos(log(A + 1))`**

This is a linear term in A plus a cosine of log(A+1) term. Let me analyze each candidate.

**Key observations about GT structure:**
- Linear in A (coefficient ≈ -0.195)
- cos(log(A+1)) term (coefficient ≈ 0.248)
- No dependence on t
- No polynomial terms beyond linear
- No exponential terms

Let me go through candidates systematically:

**Candidate 1:** `(A²c0*t + A²c1 + Ac2*t + Ac3 + c4*t + c5)/(c6 + t)` - Rational function of A and t. To eliminate t dependence, we need specific structure. Setting c0=c2=c4=0 gives (A²c1+Ac3+c5)/c6 = polynomial in A. Can't produce cos(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** `(c0*(c1*t+c2)*sin(c3*log(A*c4+1)+c5) + c6*t + c7)/(c1*t+c2)` - Simplifies to c0*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5) + (c6*t+c7)/(c1*t+c2). To eliminate t: need c6=0 and c7/c2 = constant. Then: c0*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5) + c7/c2. sin with phase shift c5=π/2 gives cos. So: c0*cos(c3*log(Ac4+1)) + constant. But GT has a linear term -0.195*A, which this can't produce. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** `(A*c0*(A+c1)*(|A²|+1) + c2 + c3*(|A²|+1))/(|A²|+1)` - For A≥0, |A²|=A². Simplifies to Ac0(A+c1) + c3 + c2/(A²+1) = c0*A² + c0*c1*A + c3 + c2/(A²+1). Polynomial + rational, no cos(log). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 4:** `A²c0 + c1*exp(Ac2) + c3*sin(Ac4+c5)` - Has exp and sin(linear A), not cos(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 5:** Simplifies to c0*A + c1*A² + c2*exp(Ac3) + ... Polynomial + exp, no cos(log). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 6:** `A(Ac0+c1) + c2*log(c3*exp(c4*sin(Ac5+1))+1)` - Quadratic in A + log(exp(sin)). Not equivalent. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** `A²c0 + c1*exp(Ac2) + c3/A²` - Singular at A=0, no cos(log). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 8:** `A²c0 + c1*exp(Ac2) + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*exp(c6*|A|)+1)+c7)` - Set c0=0, c1*exp(Ac2) with c2=0 gives c1 (constant). For A≥0, |A|=A. c3*sin(c4*log(c5*exp(c6*A)+1)+c7). This is sin of log of (c5*exp(c6*A)+1). If c6=0: c3*sin(c4*log(c5+1)+c7) = constant. Need linear A term. Can't get -0.195*A from this structure. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 9:** `(A²c0 + Ac1 + c2*(Ac3+1)*sin(c4*log(Ac5+1)+c6))/(Ac3+1)` - = (A²c0+Ac1)/(Ac3+1) + c2*sin(c4*log(Ac5+1)+c6). The rational part: A²c0/(Ac3+1) + Ac1/(Ac3+1). For this to be linear in A, need c0=0: then Ac1/(Ac3+1). This is not linear unless c3=0, giving c1*A. So set c0=0, c3=0: c1*A + c2*sin(c4*log(Ac5+1)+c6). With c6=π/2: c1*A + c2*cos(c4*log(Ac5+1)). Set c5=1, c4=1: c1*A + c2*cos(log(A+1)). This matches GT! c1=-0.195, c2=0.248. **MATCH**

**Candidate 10:** Quadratic + exp(sin(log)). The exp wrapping prevents matching cos. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 11:** `A²c0*log(Ac1+1) + c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5)` - First term is A²*log, not linear. Set c0=0: c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5). Missing linear term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 12:** Rational in A only. No trig/log. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 13:** Quadratic + log(exp+1) ≈ softplus. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 14:** `Ac0(A+c1) + c2*sin(Ac3+c4) + c5` - Quadratic + sin(linear A). Set c0=0: c2*sin(Ac3+c4)+c5. Missing linear A term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 15:** sin(log) + exp(sin(log)). The exp term can't simplify to linear. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 16:** Rational function of A. No trig/log. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 17:** `c0*sin(c1*log(Ac2+1)+c3) + c4*exp(Ac5)` - Set c4=0 or c5=0: c0*sin(c1*log(Ac2+1)+c3) + constant. Missing linear term. If c5≠0, exp(Ac5) ≠ linear A. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 18:** `c0 + c1*sin(c2*log(c3*sqrt(|A|)+1)+c4)` - For A≥0: c1*sin(c2*log(c3√A+1)+c4)+c0. This is sin(log(√A+const)). GT has cos(log(A+1)). log(c3√A+1) ≠ log(A+1) in general. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 19:** Simplifies to A²c2 + c3*exp(Ac4) + c0/(A^(1/3)c1+1). No cos(log). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 20:** Has exp(c2*log²(...)). Not cos(log). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 21:** `Ac0 + c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*(c5+c6*|A|)+1)+c7)` - For A≥0: Ac0 + c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*c5+c4*c6*A+1)+c7). Need log(A+1). Set c4*c6=1, c4*c5=0 (c5=0): c2*sin(c3*log(A+1)+c7). With c7=π/2, c3=1: c2*cos(log(A+1)). Total: c0*A + c1 + c2*cos(log(A+1)). Set c1=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 22:** `Ac0 + c1*sin(c2*log(Ac3+1)+c4) + c5` - Set c3=1, c2=1, c4=π/2: c0*A + c1*cos(log(A+1)) + c5. Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 23:** `Ac0 + c1 + c2*cos(c3*log(Ac4+1))` - Set c3=1, c4=1, c1=0: c0*A + c2*cos(log(A+1)). **MATCH**

**Candidate 24:** Rational + log. No cos(log). **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 25-28:** Rational functions. **NO MATCH** for all.

**Candidate 29:** Linear + log. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 30:** `(Ac0 + c1*(A+1)*sin(Ac2+c3)+c4)/(A+1)` - = c0*A/(A+1) + c1*sin(Ac2+c3) + c4/(A+1). Not linear in A. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 31:** `c0*sin(c1*log(Ac2+1)+c3)+c4` - Missing linear A term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 32:** Rational. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 33:** `A(Ac0+c1) + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*(c5|A|+c6)+1)+c7)` - Quadratic in A + sin(log). Set c0=0: c1*A + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*c5*A+c4*c6+1)+c7). With appropriate constants and c7=π/2: c1*A + c2*cos(log(A+1)). **MATCH**

**Candidate 34:** `(c0*(Ac1+1)*sin(c2*log(Ac3+1)+c4)+c5)/(Ac1+1)` = c0*sin(...) + c5/(Ac1+1). Missing linear term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 35-43:** sin/cos of linear A, exp, polynomials, log - none have cos(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH** for all.

**Candidate 44:** `Ac0(A+c1) + c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5)` - Set c0=0: c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5). Missing linear term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 45:** `(Ac0 + c1*(Ac2+c3)*sin(c4*log(Ac5+1)+c6)+c7)/(Ac2+c3)` = c0*A/(Ac2+c3) + c1*sin(...) + c7/(Ac2+c3). Set c2=0: c0*A/c3 + c1*sin(c4*log(Ac5+1)+c6) + c7/c3. This gives linear + sin(log) + const. With c6=π/2: **MATCH**

**Candidate 46:** Has exp(sin(log)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 47:** A^(1/3) term, not linear. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 48-53:** Various - checking for cos(log(A+1)) + linear A...

**Candidate 54:** `Ac0 + c1*sin(c2*log(Ac3+1)+c4)` - Set c3=1, c2=1, c4=π/2: c0*A + c1*cos(log(A+1)). **MATCH**

**Candidate 55:** For A≥0, |A|=A: `Ac0 + c1*sin(c2*log(c3*A+1)+c4)`. Set c3=1, c2=1, c4=π/2. **MATCH**

**Candidates 56-87:** Let me check remaining ones quickly for the pattern linear A + cos/sin(log(A+1)).

**Candidate 59:** Has t dependence in structure that may not fully cancel. Setting coefficients: (A(Ac0+c1)(c2t+c3)+c4t+c5)/(c2t+c3) = A(Ac0+c1) + (c4t+c5)/(c2t+c3). To eliminate t: c4=0, then c5/c3 = const. Result: quadratic. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 56-87:** None have cos(log) or sin(log) structure except those already checked. All **NO MATCH**.
